{"step_index":486,"source":"MODEL","type":"PLANNER_RESPONSE","status":"DONE","created_at":"2026-05-17T14:12:15Z","content":"I have found and fixed the root cause of the JIT failure!\n\nThe problem was extremely subtle and related to the ABI (Application Binary Interface) for **variadic functions on Apple Silicon (AArch64)**. \nIn the FFI test files, we declared `printf` as a fixed-arity function: `fn printf(format: *const i8, val: i32) -> i32;`\n\nWhen `lli` lowered this to LLVM IR and executed it, it passed the integer argument (`42`, `99`, `2`, etc.) in the `w1` register, according to the standard calling convention for fixed-arity functions. However, the actual C standard library implementation of `printf` is a **variadic** function (`int printf(const char *format, ...)`). On macOS Apple Silicon, variadic arguments are *never* passed in registers; they are **always passed on the stack**. \n\n<truncated 632 bytes>"}
